<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_458da51d-d1ae-4754-b049-29a96a7cb11f'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/312057-hi-everyone-i-am-trying-to-get-my-13">Hi Everyone

I am trying to get my 13 year old son to read more. Unlike me, he sees reading as a chore and not something one does as easy as breathing.

My question is: would Watchers, Twilight Eyes, Strangers and Midnight (all by Dean Koontz) be suitable for a 13 year old?

I read these books as a teen and remember not being able to put them down, but not much more than that.

Thanks in advance.

Mandy</a>
</div>

I didn't get into horror fiction until around 1987 when Stephen King's novel It came out.   <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/10064743" />
    <a title="Alejandro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro"><img alt="Alejandro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328672389p2/665584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/10064743?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alejandro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alejandro" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro">Alejandro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780425118702" href="/book/show/228206.Midnight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=novel">novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer10064743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2453071811500943564"><b>
  <u>Koontz, you did it again!</u>
</b><br/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>THE RE-ASSURANCE OF FINDING A FAVORITE AUTHOR</u>
</b><br/><br/>After my happy encounter of the great author Dean Koontz in the novel <i>Phantoms</i> (see my review of that one <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/10064722' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a>.) (back then in 1992). I knew that I want to read more books by him.<br/><br/>My second novel was this one, <i>Midnight</i>. And I am glad to say that I chosen well.<br/><br/>By then, I still wasn't able to read on English yet, so that novel I read on Spanish then. <br/><br/>At that moment I didn't know much about which novels to choose from Dean</span>
  <span id="freeText2453071811500943564" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>Koontz, you did it again!</u>
</b><br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE RE-ASSURANCE OF FINDING A FAVORITE AUTHOR</u>
</b><br /><br />After my happy encounter of the great author Dean Koontz in the novel <i>Phantoms</i> (see my review of that one <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/10064722" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.) (back then in 1992). I knew that I want to read more books by him.<br /><br />My second novel was this one, <i>Midnight</i>. And I am glad to say that I chosen well.<br /><br />By then, I still wasn't able to read on English yet, so that novel I read on Spanish then. <br /><br />At that moment I didn't know much about which novels to choose from Dean Koontz, also at that time, I depended of which titles were translated and available in the local book stores. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>KOONTZ'S TOWNS &amp; DOGS</u>
</b><br /><br />Happily, not matter of the language limitations (back then in 1992), my second choice was the perfect one after my experience with <i>Phantoms</i> since this book has one of the elements that I enjoyed the most in my reading experience of <i>Phantoms</i>, that it was how detailed, Koontz, described the town of the story. <br /><br />In <i>Phantoms</i>, he did such wonderful job describing the whole town of Snowfield, and here on <i>Midnight</i>, he did the same favor for the town of Moonlight Cove. <br /><br />During the reading experience, one is able to reach a feeling that you are there, in those towns along with the characters (humans and animals alike).<br /><br />Each character in the story is well developed with a strong background and they act according with their personalities.<br /><br />So, this book has another trademark of Koontz' style that it's having a wonderful dog with great intelligence becoming another main character with an important role in the story. <br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>KOONTZ'S HONESTY</u>
</b><br /><br />Dean Koontz got inspired to write this novel on the works of the film <i>Invasion of the Body Snatchers</i> and the book of <i>The Island of Dr. Moreau</i> and he isn't afraid of just telling so at certain point of the narrative. <br /><br />Something that also I admired of him, his honesty, since there isn't anything to be ashamed in admiting his inspirations for his own original novel.<br /><br />I hate when an author doesn't admit that he/she watched some movie or he/she read some book and saying that it's a "coincidence" the similarities on the stories. Geez! They think that readers are dumb or something? <br /><br />So, Dean Koontz doesn't even wait for later questioning, he knows that people will notice the similarities and he knows how to mention his inspiration in the middle of the story.<br /><br />Great tale of horror and suspense...<br /><br />...that keep you entertained during the whole book. <br /><br />Now, it's better to go,...<br /><br />...since <i>midnight</i> is almost upon us!<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2453071811500943564" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1823162197" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1823162197" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28602001-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438967931p2/28602001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1823162197?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/28602001-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition 9781472202833" href="/book/show/18964777-midnight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28602001-emma?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1823162197" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15811615264922676396">I unashamedly love this book. I can't even begin to count how many times i've read it. Despite being a classic horror novel, it's one of my warm blanket reads because it reminds me of the time when I was young and branching out into new genres. Dean Koontz was a library staple, I must have read his entire back catalogue. But the two that forever stayed with me were this one and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32423.Watchers' title='Watchers by Dean Koontz' rel='nofollow noopener'>Watchers</a>. I bought both right after returning the library versions and I still have those same copies today. I won't te</span>
  <span id="freeText15811615264922676396" style="display:none">I unashamedly love this book. I can't even begin to count how many times i've read it. Despite being a classic horror novel, it's one of my warm blanket reads because it reminds me of the time when I was young and branching out into new genres. Dean Koontz was a library staple, I must have read his entire back catalogue. But the two that forever stayed with me were this one and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32423.Watchers" title="Watchers by Dean Koontz" rel="nofollow noopener">Watchers</a>. I bought both right after returning the library versions and I still have those same copies today. I won't tell you how many years later it is, but it's a lot. A LOT. Recently, I happened to notice a load of his books, and those of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/83937.Richard_Laymon" title="Richard Laymon" rel="nofollow noopener">Richard Laymon</a> (another old favourite), are only 99p on Kindle UK- it was impossible to resist being able to carry them with me at all times. So: REREAD!<br /><br />Midnight is quintessential Koontz: small town, evil megalomaniac, clever animals, strong female and male lead characters, atmospheric weather (fog and more fog), corrupt law or bureaucracy, and finally...terrifying creatures running around in the dark ripping people to shreds. It's giving me a rosy glow of nostalgia just writing that list out. Yet one of the surprising issues of this 1989 novel is how is stands up now. Not just the sometimes cheesy, but always brilliant writing style of the author, but the themes of man vs nature, man vs his own nature, man vs technology that form the basis for this story. It hits on so many of the deepest fears we can hold: loss of our humanity; being forced into the role of prey, chased in the dark by unknown predators; not knowing who is friend or foe; indiscriminate death, where even children aren't safe; the sometimes incomprehensible, almost alien forms of technological innovation...<br /><br />On top of all that, it's got that perfect mix of silly and scary. You know, of course, that the goodies will save the day but before that you have to cope with the voices of the Regressives, their whispery, desperate needy tone.... *shudder*... I dare anyone to read this book and then go outside in the dark without repeatedly checking their surroundings and jumping at every noise.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15811615264922676396" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1706314944" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1706314944" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16796020-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452866952p2/16796020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1706314944?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/16796020-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780425118702" href="/book/show/228206.Midnight">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1706314944" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5602531896266135853">This is classic Koontz. Strong heroine/ female protagonist, super smart dog, sociopathic/megalomaniacal antagonist, science gone horribly wrong, a group of people have to save the day, blossoming romance between seemingly opposite characters, a small town, California setting and a good yet, corny ending lol. <br/>The blending of horror and science fiction is superb. Koontz is so good at mixing the two genres with a dash of thriller/suspense to tie it all together. <br/>The creatures that are in this book </span>
  <span id="freeText5602531896266135853" style="display:none">This is classic Koontz. Strong heroine/ female protagonist, super smart dog, sociopathic/megalomaniacal antagonist, science gone horribly wrong, a group of people have to save the day, blossoming romance between seemingly opposite characters, a small town, California setting and a good yet, corny ending lol. <br />The blending of horror and science fiction is superb. Koontz is so good at mixing the two genres with a dash of thriller/suspense to tie it all together. <br />The creatures that are in this book are cool and I like the fictional scientific explanation for their existence. They give this book a monster movie type of vibe. <br />This book reminded me a little of Invasion of the Body Snatchers which is a great thing seeing as how I love the original film and its idea. <br />The storyline is interesting and Koontz makes the terror and science behind the danger seem feasible especially in today's highly technological society. <br />There is an abundance of social commentary being made here. What really makes us human? Is it our emotions? Intellect? Or is it something else entirely? How far would we go to achieve a sense of perfection? If we lack all emotions, are we even human anymore? Are we too reliant on technology? Can this reliance eventually come back to haunt us? What is the true meaning and purpose of life? These are all very relevant, thought provoking questions and I feel that they are even more prevalent now in this current technology heavy and dependent world than ever before and especially more than when this book was written. I feel like Koontz might have been able to see into the future a bit and see how much technology would play a major role in our lives and livelihoods. <br />The characters are good. My favorite character was the disabled Vietnam vet, Harry. Koontz does a good job of making empathetic characters that you want to root for and helps us to see from the twisted perspective of the antagonist and at least see where they are coming from or why they think they have to do what they're doing even if it seems completely wrong or insane to us as the readers. <br />Koontz throws in several horror and science fiction movie references that a die hard fan like myself really appreciated. It even feels a little like a B movie at times. <br />The small town setting in horror fiction is one of my favorite literary tropes and the town of Moonlight Cove is crafted well. I immediately got to know the town and what it was all about as well as a little about the places it contained and some of the people that lived there. <br />The pace is good, it ramps us when it needs to but otherwise it is very steady and moves along well for an almost 500 page book. <br />I love Koontz's writing style. It's very descriptive in parts and it has a stylized nature to it that lends itself to some speculation and thought provocation as to the picture he is painting for us and the story he is telling and simply put, it just works. Having read quite a few of his books, I have come to appreciate his writing style very much and I greatly enjoy pointing out and/or noticing the various Koontzisms located within his works. <br />The third part/act of the book is a thrill ride and thunders along as soon as shit starts to hit the fan. The conclusion was a nice way to end the novel although it was corny but that's Koontz's style so I was cool with it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5602531896266135853" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_224607014" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="J.S. Bailey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5281321-j-s-bailey"><img alt="J.S. Bailey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570121244p2/5281321.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/224607014?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.S. Bailey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.S. Bailey" href="/user/show/5281321-j-s-bailey">J.S. Bailey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer224607014" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6857004604282426589">This is one of Koontz's better novels--totally creepy, and totally awesome. Plus, the afterword at the end made me giggle.<br/><br/>The reason this novel resonated so strongly with me is because I can identify with the residents of Moonlight Cove who were losing touch with their emotions. There was a time a few years ago when I suffered from extreme depression and anxiety. I was prescribed an antidepressant, and lo and behold, the depression went away!<br/><br/>But so did everything else. I felt no joy. No happines</span>
  <span id="freeText6857004604282426589" style="display:none">This is one of Koontz's better novels--totally creepy, and totally awesome. Plus, the afterword at the end made me giggle.<br /><br />The reason this novel resonated so strongly with me is because I can identify with the residents of Moonlight Cove who were losing touch with their emotions. There was a time a few years ago when I suffered from extreme depression and anxiety. I was prescribed an antidepressant, and lo and behold, the depression went away!<br /><br />But so did everything else. I felt no joy. No happiness. I wasn't necessarily sad, either. I just existed in a bland emotional state that bordered between Blah and What's the Point? I finally became so frustrated with my lack of feeling that I quit taking my medicine against doctor's orders. I've been fine ever since. (Disclaimer: I didn't quit "cold turkey," so if you're in the same boat I was in, please at least slowly wean yourself off of your meds so nothing bad happens.)<br /><br />In Midnight when Loman Watkins laments to Thomas Shaddack that life is basically meaningless without emotions and the pleasures that come with them, I was thinking, "Holy crap! YES!!!"<br /><br />So, Mr. Koontz, congratulations for successfully touching my heart. :) </span>
  <a data-text-id="6857004604282426589" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText11235614191579453972" style="display:none">This was the February 2011 and April 2017 Group Read in the Koontzland - Dean Koontz Group<br />I've read Midnight 3 times. <br /><br />Midnight has never been one of my favorites, but it is a solid &amp; intriguing story. I find many similarities between Midnight and Dean Koontz's Frankenstein Series - the ideas of control &amp; improvements upon human conditions getting out of control.<br /><br />A funny quote:<br />". . . . had so many corn-chip crumbs sprinkled across the front of her royal-blue sweater that she appeared to be breading herself with the intention of going into the kitchen, climbing into an oven, and <i>becoming</i> food."<br />-Midnight, Chapter 12<br /><br />A favorite quote:<br />"Even as a child, she had preferred night to day, had enjoyed sitting out in the yard after sunset, under the star-speckled sky listening to frogs and crickets. Darkness soothed. It softened the sharp edges of the world, toned down the too-harsh colors. With the coming of twilight, the sky seemed to recede; the universe expanded. The night was bigger than the day, and in its realm, life seemed to have more possibilities."<br />-Midnight, Chapter One</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3247951213232959979">I want to comment on this because I really didn't care for it, but my late wife loved this and some other Koontz books that I don't care for (at least as much). So in honer of her I gave it 3 stars recognizing that there will be people who like some of this writer's books while others don't. I note that many of the ones I don't care for both my wife and daughter like. But, I can't really build on that as my daughter and I liked The Taking, and my wife didn't...sigh. Go figure. All I can suggest </span>
  <span id="freeText3247951213232959979" style="display:none">I want to comment on this because I really didn't care for it, but my late wife loved this and some other Koontz books that I don't care for (at least as much). So in honer of her I gave it 3 stars recognizing that there will be people who like some of this writer's books while others don't. I note that many of the ones I don't care for both my wife and daughter like. But, I can't really build on that as my daughter and I liked The Taking, and my wife didn't...sigh. Go figure. All I can suggest here is try his books yourself. He has written some I'd list as up there in my top...oh 20 to 50 books and others I find not so great.<br /><br />The plot in this one is a good idea. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ It's an earlier version of the nanobot holocaust novel. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The problem I have with it is that it tends to go over the top. It put me in mind of some horror movies I've seen where the "horror" went so over the top that it moved into dark humor. I think you'll see what I mean when/if you read this one. It's not bad but it is going to appeal to some readers more than others. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13452543141628231916">Could humanity be "improved" if more like machines and devoid of emotions? That is the premise of the bad guy in this thriller. He is trying to convert the humans of Moonlight Cove. Standing against him are an FBI agent, disillusioned with life; a woman who came to Moonlight Cove, suspicious of her sister's death; a disabled veteran whose view of responsibility questions the values of Shaddack (the bad guy): an 11-year-old girl who has lost her parents due to the conversion and of course a lovab</span>
  <span id="freeText13452543141628231916" style="display:none">Could humanity be "improved" if more like machines and devoid of emotions? That is the premise of the bad guy in this thriller. He is trying to convert the humans of Moonlight Cove. Standing against him are an FBI agent, disillusioned with life; a woman who came to Moonlight Cove, suspicious of her sister's death; a disabled veteran whose view of responsibility questions the values of Shaddack (the bad guy): an 11-year-old girl who has lost her parents due to the conversion and of course a lovable, loyal lab who brings affection and love to the good guys. This is one of Koontz's best as he explores the nature of what it means to be human and the constant battle of good vs. evil.</span>

<div id="review_140822857" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/140822857" />
    <a title="Brett" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/436346-brett"><img alt="Brett" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1195094919p2/436346.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/140822857?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brett" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brett" href="/user/show/436346-brett">Brett</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/436346-brett?shelf=popular-fiction">popular-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/436346-brett?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer140822857" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13947299141084741034">Review contains spoilers. This novel by Dean Koontz sports a lot of Koontz's usual tropes. Among them are: the good-hearted protagonist that has experienced a loss, the angelic and unrealistically mature child, the unnecessary romance between main characters in the midst of mayhem, the remorseless mad scientist, the cute dog, and the easily predictable horror/sci-fi premise. Reading Koontz is too often like reading a screenplay for a March release Hollywood film--just very little complexity or s</span>
  <span id="freeText13947299141084741034" style="display:none">Review contains spoilers. This novel by Dean Koontz sports a lot of Koontz's usual tropes. Among them are: the good-hearted protagonist that has experienced a loss, the angelic and unrealistically mature child, the unnecessary romance between main characters in the midst of mayhem, the remorseless mad scientist, the cute dog, and the easily predictable horror/sci-fi premise. Reading Koontz is too often like reading a screenplay for a March release Hollywood film--just very little complexity or surprises.<br /><br />That said, this is far from the worst Koontz book I've read. I give it two stars primarily because of two scenes that I thought employed effective visuals--one is at the opening of the book, the other a curious close-call with one of the book's creatures. <br /><br />But there are way too many gaffes to give Midnight any sort of recommendation. From page 104: "Harry stared at the apelike countenance, thought it was leaner and uglier and more fierce and infinitely stranger than the face of an ape." This sort of writing makes me crazy. Infinitely stranger than the face of an ape? That phrase has exactly zero meaning. Or from page 108, when a cry in the distance is described as "shrill yet guttural." Koontz does this kind of thing all the time--he was tall yet short, the sound was loud yet quiet. A good writer can give a description of the uncanny without resorting to nonsense.<br /><br />I need to add something about a serious plot hole as well. The plot of this book has most of the citizens of a small town being changed to so-called "New People" in an experiment of which they are unwilling members. These New People are animalistic in that they live for essentially food and sexual pleasure only. Some of the New People embrace their wildness and go nuts. Others are worried and perplexed about losing their emotions. But none of those that loses their emotions ever ventures outside the community to seek help. Instead, the whole town gets turned over the course of a couple weeks with no one ever saying anything. If I thought my humanity had been stolen by a local mad scientist, I would hope some equally enterprising scientist elsewhere might be able to give it back to me. But what do I know?<br /><br />Finally, one last thing I must bring up. The maudlin concluding scene of the novel is unbearable. The protagonist Sam is bitter at the beginning of the novel because he has had a near death experience and didn't like what he saw on the other side. What horrible thing comes after death that Sam saw, we wonder. Tessa, his love interest, brings Sam around to the life-affirming viewpoint that all Koontz characters are required to hold by the novel's end. The big reveal is that Sam was upset to see that there is an afterlife of some kind--you see, he hated living so much that he was mad that he would keep living. If that isn't the lamest plot point you've across, then God help you. Anyway, now Sam is on-board again with loving being alive, and he and Tessa return to his home where Sam hopes to make amends with his estranged teenage son. How does he do this? In the "touching" final scene, Sam destroys his son's rock n' roll albums. One of the strangest scenes of unintentional satire I have come across.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13947299141084741034" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2704056415" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2704056415" />
    <a title="Andrew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/800291-andrew"><img alt="Andrew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1295167791p2/800291.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2704056415?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew" href="/user/show/800291-andrew">Andrew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/43550759-midnight">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2704056415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14211661734043144385">Okay - does this count as a guilty pleasure? <br/><br/>Let me explain I had moved away and was renting a house while attending university - where I first found out that people can like the same books as I do. At the same time a local book shop was starting on a promotion of Dean Koontz thrillers (some with a supernatural or at least unconventional edge).<br/><br/>To tie in with this the publisher had lunched an ad campaign that used the foiled covers. I was lucky enough to sweet talk the staff in to letting me havi</span>
  <span id="freeText14211661734043144385" style="display:none">Okay - does this count as a guilty pleasure? <br /><br />Let me explain I had moved away and was renting a house while attending university - where I first found out that people can like the same books as I do. At the same time a local book shop was starting on a promotion of Dean Koontz thrillers (some with a supernatural or at least unconventional edge).<br /><br />To tie in with this the publisher had lunched an ad campaign that used the foiled covers. I was lucky enough to sweet talk the staff in to letting me having them when the finished. So why the importance - well up to that point I didn't really know much about Dean Knootz just I loved the covers. However ironically a local store was selling off his hardback editions cheap this being one of them.<br /><br />So why not I though - and not only was introduced to the world of Dean Koontz but also the dubious pleasure of reading through the night and in to the morning. Yep I missed lectures to catch up sleep after reading this book cover to cover through the night. <br /><br />Well here I am 20(ahem) years later and still totally engrossed with this book. Yes Mr Koontz's books rise and fall from favour - the covers change and the comparisons to other authors continues but I can still pick up this book and want to read it from cover to cover in one go. <br /><br />The story is pretty straight forward - the action linear and the characters predictable - but who cares its great fun and right up to the last scene a rip roaring ride. Okay I am sure there are better and more challenging books by Dean but still I count this (along with Lightening and Watchers) and one of my favourite books of his. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14211661734043144385" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10478757824786256579" style="display:none">Moonlight Cove California and his population are suffering from inexplicable and horrific mutations!!!<br />Gruesome and mysterious shapes dart trough the night, leaving behind bloody tracks....<br /><br />Then we have an undercover agent trying to overcame his personal demons, trapped desperately in the city... and while fleeing from unspeakable horrendously and malicious enemies he try to discover the reason to this nightmare....<br /><br />Also a young girl that has seen too much, will be mercilessly haunted by her personal loss, and must cope with an hostile environment watching and seeking after her....<br /><br />Here lives a young Vietnam veteran too, which due to his injuries is dependent on his wheelchair...<br />Alone in his flat his only companion a Labrador and trough his telescope nights watching and registering the changes that Moonlight Cove is undergoing.....<br /><br />Friends I love this novel, written grippingly and with a rich descriptive prose!!!<br />Let me say it clearly: one of the bests by Koontzt.....<br /><br />Powerful written, a true page turner!!!<br /><br />Dean;D<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1087268564" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1087268564" />
    <a title="Siobhan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35855553-siobhan"><img alt="Siobhan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510311895p2/35855553.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1087268564?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Siobhan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Siobhan" href="/user/show/35855553-siobhan">Siobhan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781472230294" href="/book/show/24517370-midnight">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1087268564" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12207926300118342121">This is yet another wonderful Koontz read.<br/><br/>I say this with most of my Koontz reads: my views are probably somewhat bias, considering how he is my favourite author. Oh, he is far from perfect. There are times when I have disliked (never hated, merely disliked) what he has written. But as a whole, he has rarely done me wrong. Thus, whenever I see a Koontz book I have yet to read I grab it. Such being the case with Midnight. <br/><br/>I’m not sure when or why, but as of late I’ve been noticing that Koontz’s o</span>
  <span id="freeText12207926300118342121" style="display:none">This is yet another wonderful Koontz read.<br /><br />I say this with most of my Koontz reads: my views are probably somewhat bias, considering how he is my favourite author. Oh, he is far from perfect. There are times when I have disliked (never hated, merely disliked) what he has written. But as a whole, he has rarely done me wrong. Thus, whenever I see a Koontz book I have yet to read I grab it. Such being the case with Midnight. <br /><br />I’m not sure when or why, but as of late I’ve been noticing that Koontz’s older books are being released with new covers. Due to this, they are often ending up in stores that sell the recent releases at a discounted price. As I’m not one to turn down a good bargain, I have been jumping upon theses finds as they come about. With Midnight, my excitement was somewhat more than it has been with some of his other books. Midnight had, after all, spent quite some time sitting on my to-read list. I would have worked my way around to it in the end – there was no doubt of that – yet finding it going cheap pushed it up my list.<br /><br />Unfortunately, my reading of the story was not as straightforward as it should have been. If anything, it was a lesson in why I shouldn’t read books I’m excited about whilst travelling. Oh, I had plenty of time. My journey home is about ten hours, after all. Sadly, the journey turned into a nightmare. Whilst it gave me more time to read – added hours onto a journey have tiny benefits, even if we do not see them at the time – the fact that it was the middle of the night and the reading lights stopped working meant I couldn’t read as much as this as I wanted to.<br /><br />Thus, my start to the story was not what it should have been.<br /><br />Oh, I was pulled in – but I was unable to work through as much of it as I wanted to. As always when my journey turns into a nightmare, I really wasn’t up for reading the next couple of days. I wanted to catch up on sleep. Then there was family to see, and a birthday to have. All of it amounted to be book being read in fits and starts. Much to my dismay, every time something good was happening I was pulled away. It seemed as though I was destined never to finish the story.<br /><br />In the end, however, I put my foot down. I couldn’t take it anymore. How dare people stop me from reading my favourite author! How dare people interrupt a truly engaging story! Thus, I locked myself away until I had finished the couple of hundreds of pages I had left.<br /><br />Oh how glad I was!<br /><br />As always, Koontz weaves a wonderful tale. With his usual proses and twists and turns, the tale is a wonderful one – even when read across days with just a chapter or two here and there, as I was forced to experience it. You’re pulled into the world, and you cannot help but want the best for the characters. There are the odd Koontz cliché to be seen here and there – but overall, it’s a wonderful read. Whilst not my favourite, I did enjoy it.<br /><br />More than worth it if you’re a Koontz fan.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12207926300118342121" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText394350630349869061" style="display:none">This was another good read from Koontz. Grips you from the beginning and gets stranger and more intriguing from there.<br /><br /><b>Publisher's Summary</b><br /><br />In picturesque Moonlight Cove, California, inexplicable deaths occur, and spine-tingling terror descends to this edge of paradise. Growing numbers of residents harbor a secret so dark it is sure to cost even more lives.<br /><br />Tessa Lockland comes to town to probe her sister's seemingly unprompted suicide. Independent and clever, she meets up with Sam Booker, an undercover FBI agent sent to Moonlight Cove to discover the truth behind the mysterious deaths.<br /><br />They meet Harry Talbot, a wheelchair-bound veteran, who has seen things from his window that he was not meant to see. Together they begin to understand the depth of evil in Moonlight Cove. Chrissie Foster, a resourceful 11-year-old, running from parents who have suddenly changed and in whom darkness dwells, joins them. Together they make a stand against darkness and terror.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer975671026539484606">Warning this review contains spoilers<br/><br/><br/>I read this book as part of a group read for the month of April, for the Koontzland group. I found this book really enjoyable, it's a typical Koontz book that mixes science fiction and horror with a hint of conspiracy theory fiction. If I was asked who would I recommend this book to it would be fans of the x files.<br/>The book starts off with strange deaths, murders and suicides, but what's even stranger is the way in which the bodies are disposed of by the autho</span>
  <span id="freeText975671026539484606" style="display:none">Warning this review contains spoilers<br /><br /><br />I read this book as part of a group read for the month of April, for the Koontzland group. I found this book really enjoyable, it's a typical Koontz book that mixes science fiction and horror with a hint of conspiracy theory fiction. If I was asked who would I recommend this book to it would be fans of the x files.<br />The book starts off with strange deaths, murders and suicides, but what's even stranger is the way in which the bodies are disposed of by the authorities. This is brought to the attention of the FBI by a disabled Vietnam vet, also a woman appears in the town to find out what really happened to her sister and a young girl comes home early from school and notices something is very wrong with her parents and a chase ensues. Finally we are introduced to the books bad guy a genius who is basically a crazed lunatic who wants to speed up evolution. Things start to go horribly wrong and unforeseen side effects completely destroy the plan.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer27497097" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2406423687946939010">This is my favorite Koontz novel, although it's very close to Phantoms. I think this is a lesson in how a thriller should be written. Just a wonderful work.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_404530897" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/404530897" />
    <a title="jade" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11030012-jade"><img alt="jade" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562419355p2/11030012.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/404530897?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jade" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jade" href="/user/show/11030012-jade">jade</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780425118702" href="/book/show/228206.Midnight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11030012-jade?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer404530897" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17859313724005566024"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/228206.Midnight' title='Midnight by Dean Koontz' rel='nofollow noopener'> Midnight</a> is the kind of book that I want to read whenever I turn towards <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9355.Dean_Koontz' title='Dean Koontz' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dean Koontz</a>. It’s a light, clichéd but horrendously frightening read, and this particular work of Koontz also includes a bit of philosophical thinking on the side, mainly on what exactly makes a human a human.<br/><br/>Change is abound in the small town of Moonlight Cove, where its inhabitants are slowly transformed into wild and savage beasts against their own will. Four main characters investigate the cause of these ungodly transf</span>
  <span id="freeText17859313724005566024" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/228206.Midnight" title="Midnight by Dean Koontz" rel="nofollow noopener"> Midnight</a> is the kind of book that I want to read whenever I turn towards <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9355.Dean_Koontz" title="Dean Koontz" rel="nofollow noopener">Dean Koontz</a>. It’s a light, clichéd but horrendously frightening read, and this particular work of Koontz also includes a bit of philosophical thinking on the side, mainly on what exactly makes a human a human.<br /><br />Change is abound in the small town of Moonlight Cove, where its inhabitants are slowly transformed into wild and savage beasts against their own will. Four main characters investigate the cause of these ungodly transformations: undercover FBI-agent Sam Booker, originally sent to investigate a string of mysterious murders; Tessa Lockland, searching for the reason behind her sister’s death; disabled veteran Harry Talbot and his faithful dog, who catch frightening glimpses of the town’s citizens’ changes; and Chrissie Foster, a young girl who narrowly escaped a deathly attack of her own parents after they forcefully transformed into something she’s unable to describe. Behind it all is, of course, a scientific yet criminal mastermind, who is equally creepy as the transforming townsfolk.<br /><br />As I mentioned earlier, this book is definitely not without its clichés, but I appreciate it for its dynamic tension, action, and suspense. Sam Booker and Tessa Lockland are pretty much cardboard cut-outs, but Harry Talbot and the young girl Chrissie bring something interesting to the table (even though it’s nothing that hasn’t been done before; the wise old man, and the girl who’s unbelievably smart for her age). I enjoyed Talbot and his dog the most, eventually. The horror is also pretty well-done, and a certain scene involving a boy and his computer is something that I’ll not soon forget. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/228206.Midnight" title="Midnight by Dean Koontz" rel="nofollow noopener"> Midnight</a> is a quick horror-read that sets off speedily, riddled with disgusting transformations, and also has a crazy scientist who uses technology for his own ideological yet disturbing ideas. Recommended for both fans of Koontz and fans of horror.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17859313724005566024" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_88720511" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/88720511" />
    <a title="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction"><img alt="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605816027p2/2905339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/88720511?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" href="/user/show/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction">Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer88720511" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16305035159611235546">This is one of Dean Koontz's earlier novels and originally written in 1989. I was only 19 when I originally read it, boy, that makes me feel old! I'm reread it on unabridged audio recently. Despite its age it still holds up pretty well as a straight up horror novel where the citizens of a nice little town turn into horrifying blood-lusty creatures all thanks to a power-hungry geeky rich madman. Come to think of it, this is even scarier stuff in this day and age . . .<br/><br/>Anyway, I enjoyed it a lot an</span>
  <span id="freeText16305035159611235546" style="display:none">This is one of Dean Koontz's earlier novels and originally written in 1989. I was only 19 when I originally read it, boy, that makes me feel old! I'm reread it on unabridged audio recently. Despite its age it still holds up pretty well as a straight up horror novel where the citizens of a nice little town turn into horrifying blood-lusty creatures all thanks to a power-hungry geeky rich madman. Come to think of it, this is even scarier stuff in this day and age . . .<br /><br />Anyway, I enjoyed it a lot and loved the back cover picture of Dean and his beautiful golden friend. Back to the contents, the computer technology is very dated. The fact that the hero has to search high and low for a public telephone to call headquarters really brought that fact home. It's amazing to see how far things have come since 1989. If only one could go back in time and be able to eat in a restaurant without hearing little musical ditties buzzing away in every corner. I know, I know, I sound more like a grandma everyday.<br /><br />Like many a Koontz novel this one does go on (and on) a wee bit too long but it's a minor complaint as it kept me entertained without wanting to put it down never to be picked up again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16305035159611235546" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2131926258" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2131926258" />
    <a title="Ryan Lieske" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5889533-ryan-lieske"><img alt="Ryan Lieske" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517774269p2/5889533.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2131926258?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ryan Lieske" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ryan Lieske" href="/user/show/5889533-ryan-lieske">Ryan Lieske</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5889533-ryan-lieske?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5889533-ryan-lieske?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2131926258" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1198669178203894651">As I've stated in a previous review, I've never been a huge fan of Koontz. I've generally liked everything I've read by him, but there's never been anything that's truly blown me away. In 2017, I decided to do a Koontz binge, to see if I could remedy that. <br/><br/>From what I've gathered, "Midnight" is considered by many to be one of his best. And I can see why. It's a hell of a fun read. <br/><br/>My only qualms, and they're minor ones, are ones that I generally have with Koontz: the books was perhaps a little t</span>
  <span id="freeText1198669178203894651" style="display:none">As I've stated in a previous review, I've never been a huge fan of Koontz. I've generally liked everything I've read by him, but there's never been anything that's truly blown me away. In 2017, I decided to do a Koontz binge, to see if I could remedy that. <br /><br />From what I've gathered, "Midnight" is considered by many to be one of his best. And I can see why. It's a hell of a fun read. <br /><br />My only qualms, and they're minor ones, are ones that I generally have with Koontz: the books was perhaps a little too long and repetitious; his similes make me roll my eyes sometimes; and the secrets of the mystery are either too predictable, or revealed way too early. But that's just me. I know that Koontz's books are thrillers first and foremost, and maybe I'm just looking for more horror and mystery. <br /><br />If someone were to ask me for a fun, violent read, with a bit of SF thrown in, I wouldn't hesitate to recommend "Midnight." But I probably won't ever read it again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1198669178203894651" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer530024293" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13199538231093773776">This book grabbed my attention right from the beginning! The last really good book by Dean Koontz that I'd read is Watchers, and I loved that one. I just think it's incredible how one author can put so many different emotions into his books, to me, that's a good writer. There are times he's got you on the edge of your seat or biting your nails in horror, and times when he's got you laughing out loud.<br/><br/><br/>I had read a lot of the reviews on Midnight and I see that some people loved it, others not so mu</span>
  <span id="freeText13199538231093773776" style="display:none">This book grabbed my attention right from the beginning! The last really good book by Dean Koontz that I'd read is Watchers, and I loved that one. I just think it's incredible how one author can put so many different emotions into his books, to me, that's a good writer. There are times he's got you on the edge of your seat or biting your nails in horror, and times when he's got you laughing out loud.<br /><br /><br />I had read a lot of the reviews on Midnight and I see that some people loved it, others not so much, so I thought I'd give it a shot and I haven't come back disappointed. I gotta put Midnight right up there with his best, a real page turner!</span>

<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32433.The_Key_to_Midnight"><img alt="The Key to Midnight" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1348697141l/32433._SY160_.jpg" />

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oPdxY/JNKeDy+slVXgj84Z7PbW1lWfrcmHaZuQRkWdO3TwmC2G1a+ldwAQDchbfsFqwV9lSHiTB/WwWJ/sLQFg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('V8SDbVXNx4IsSosNMk2nX9D/EaGVRzK4edDSPMOaGipAfPuMf+20mInAQ1iwwOxSWJxpOqSZQVSe/U4MOTyT7w==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

The night was bigger than the day, and in its realm, life seemed to have more possibilities.&rdquo;</span>
